  //<![CDATA[
    function loadScript(url, callback) {
      var script = document.createElement("script");
      script.type = "text/javascript";
    
      if (script.readyState) {  //Internet Explorer
          script.onreadystatechange = function() {
            if (script.readyState == "loaded" ||
                    script.readyState == "complete") {
              script.onreadystatechange = null;
              callback();
            }
          };
      } else {  //Other browsers
        script.onload = function() {
          callback();
        };
      }
    
      script.src = url;
      document.getElementsByTagName("head")[0].appendChild(script);
    }
    
    function initAppleId() {
      AppleID.auth.init({
        clientId : 'com.goodreads.app', 
        scope : 'name email',
        redirectURI: 'https://www.goodreads.com/apple_users/sign_in_with_apple_web',
        state: 'apple_oauth_state_c11cafc1-42ef-4bf3-96b5-823609d91841'
      });
    }
    
    var initializeSiwa = function() {
      var APPLE_SIGN_IN_JS_URL =  "https://appleid.cdn-apple.com/appleauth/static/jsapi/appleid/1/en_US/appleid.auth.js"

<span id="freeTextContainer17646201809060689868"><i>Swallow, Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them ‘til they’ve time to grow.   <span id="freeText17646201809060689868" style="display:none"><i>Swallow, Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them ‘til they’ve time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, ‘til the hour. You won’t speak and you won’t tell, you won’t call on heav’n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, Daughter. Stay alive.</i><br /> <br />The day my mother was killed, she told my father I wouldn’t speak again, and she told him if I died, he would die too. Then she predicted the king would trade his soul and lose his son to the sky.<br /><br />My father has a claim to the throne, and he is waiting in the shadows for all of my mother’s words to come to pass. He wants desperately to be king, and I just want to be free.<br /><br />But freedom will require escape, and I’m a prisoner of my mother’s curse and my father’s greed. I can’t speak or make a sound, and I can’t wield a sword or beguile a king. In a land purged of enchantment, love might be the only magic left, and who could ever love . . . a bird?</span>

<div class='communityQuestion'>
<div class='questionText'>
<a href="/questions/1148222-i-want-to-read-this-book-but-hesitant">I want to read this book but hesitant because I saw a review on amazon that it was really more of a romance book.. I don&#39;t do the romance genre so to those who have read it.. am I wasting my time?</a>
</div>
<div class='communityQAFooter questionFooter'>
<ul class='questionFooterActions'>
<li class='footerItem like'>
<span class='likeItContainer' id='like_container_community_question_1148222'><a rel="nofollow" class="jsLike like_it" href="https://www.goodreads.com/user/new?remember=true&amp;return_url=%2Fbook%2Fshow%2F29008738-the-bird-and-the-sword">like</a></span>

</li>
<li class='footerItem communityQuestionPermalink'>
<a href="/questions/1148222-i-want-to-read-this-book-but-hesitant">See all 2 answers</a>
</li>

<div class='allCommunityAnswers'>
<div class='communityAnswer'>
<div class='communityAnswerBody'>
<div class='answererUserIcon'>
<a class="leftAlignedImage userPhoto" href="/user/show/30344620-kelsey"><img alt="" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/users/1515900018i/30344620._UY100_CR16,0,100,100_.jpg" /></a>
</div>
<div class='communityAnswerTextContainer'>
<span class='communityAnswererName'>
<a href="/user/show/30344620-kelsey">Kelsey</a>
</span>
<span class='communityAnswerText'>
<span class="expandableContainer"><span class="truncatedContent">I'd say it's about 50/50. More accurately, you could say it's fantasy with a strong focus on the relationship between the two main characters. It's no<a class="jsShow showAction" href="#">…more</a></span><span class="fullContent">I'd say it's about 50/50. More accurately, you could say it's fantasy with a strong focus on the relationship between the two main characters. It's not "romance" in the sense that you have a half-baked plot that has a bunch of hot-and-heavy scenes (actually, the sex scenes are pretty tasteful/mild compared to many in this genre). It mainly focuses on the magic, the intrigue/war of the fantasy realm, and the relationships forged from all of this. <a class="jsHide hideAction" href="#">(less)</a></span></span>
</span>
</div>
</div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1646756858" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2639673382131461678">Amy Harmon never disappoints. I thought maybe she'd disappoint with this one because I'm not into fantasy, but she didn't. Now I can't say I'm not into fantasy. Thanks, Amy. Great. Just one more genre I have to add to my list of things to read. Do me a favor and stop taking risks, okay? It's making my life busier. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_2678454881" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2678454881" />
    <a title="Miranda Reads" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads"><img alt="Miranda Reads" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1592243041p2/71848701.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2678454881?book_show_action=true">Jan 23, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Miranda Reads" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Miranda Reads" href="/user/show/71848701-miranda-reads">Miranda Reads</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=audiobook">audiobook</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/71848701-miranda-reads?shelf=ya-series">ya-series</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2678454881" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10803924682670728992"><i>
  <b>Read this one for TCE Book Club!</b>
</i><blockquote>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567360541i/28084911._SY540_.jpg' width='400' height='400' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</blockquote><b>I can forgive a lot of things, but outright stupidity is not one of them.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I have loved you every moment of every day, and I will love you until I cease to be. Bird, man, or king, I love you, and I will always love you.</i>
</blockquote> Lark is born into a world of magic, and <b>the world <i>hates </i>magic.</b><br/><br/>Legend has it that there were only a few original magic weavers: Spinners, Changers, Tellers, Healers (etc), and when they had children, those children inherited their magic. <br/><br/>A</span>
  <span id="freeText10803924682670728992" style="display:none"><i>
  <b>Read this one for TCE Book Club!</b>
</i><blockquote>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1567360541i/28084911._SY540_.jpg" width="400" height="400" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</blockquote><b>I can forgive a lot of things, but outright stupidity is not one of them.</b><blockquote>
  <i>I have loved you every moment of every day, and I will love you until I cease to be. Bird, man, or king, I love you, and I will always love you.</i>
</blockquote> Lark is born into a world of magic, and <b>the world <i>hates </i>magic.</b><br><br>Legend has it that there were only a few original magic weavers: Spinners, Changers, Tellers, Healers (etc), and when they had children, those children inherited their magic. <br><br>And over time, the magic changed and grew as the generations mixed and the magic wove in and out of society. Everyone in "modern" times has a slight twist on that original magic. <br><br>Lark is a Teller, someone who can speak and magic will make their words come true...only she cannot speak anymore, not since her mother died in Lark's place and cursed her to silence.<blockquote>
  <i>Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them 'til they've time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, 'til the hour. You won't speak and you won't tell, you won't call on heav'n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, daughter. Stay alive.</i>
</blockquote> If anyone ever finds out what she could do (or used to do), Lark will be instantly killed.<br><br>But, through a chance encounter with the current king, Lark is swept into the palace where the stakes are higher and the consequences ever more deadly. Will she survive and escape? Does she even want to?<br><br>So.<br><br>Sooooooooooo.<br><br>Soooooooooooooooooooooo.<br><br>Don't you just <b>HATE</b> it when <b>ONE</b> character ruins <b>
  <i>
    <u>EVERYTHING?</u>
  </i>
</b><br><br>Yes. I'm looking at you, Lark. <br><br>Little-Miss-Woe-Is-Me. <br><br>Little-Miss-I'm-Not-Gonna-Listen.<br><br>Little-Miss-I'm-So-Stupid-How-Am-I-STILL-Alive<br><br>The world of the <b>Bird and the Sword is stunning - </b>it has a very old-world feel but is completely fleshed out and engaging. <br><br>This world is so beautifully written that it almost (almost) makes up for the terrible-ness of Lark.<br><br><b>But, surely she can't be<i> that</i> bad...Right?</b>...it's probably a good thing you are sitting down. Cause we about to get ranty.<br><br><b>
  <u>Lark's Stupiditiy - <i>aka is that a bad idea? Imma do it.</i></u>
</b><br><br>I could barely read this book,<b>
  <i> my eyes were rolling so hard.</i>
</b><blockquote>
  <i> I swallowed, suddenly close to tears. Then why does no one see me? </i>
</blockquote>Essentially, Lark spends her whole life shut away, "unseen" if you will because of reasons. <br><br>Much to her surprise, and mine, she's able to use a Teller's powers once she begins to read. Because reasons. <br><br>She is so blown away by the power that she then practices magic.<br><br>Constantly.<br><br>She practices in her room (leaving obvious traces for her maids to find), on people walking by, on nobles in the castle (etc)...<br><br>And then she's all <b>shocked and confused</b> when there are consequences.<br><br>Gurl.<br><br>Guuuuuuuuurl please.<br><br> You've lived in this country all your life - you know that the death penalty is <b>INCREDIBLY </b>common for practicing any form of magic.<br><br>Annnnnnd then she nearly suffocates the king and laughs (drunk on her own power)? <b>To. The. King.</b><br><br>It's really a wonder he didn't execute her. <br><br><b>
  <u>The Wimpiness - <i>aka I'm just a limp noodle</i></u>
</b> <br><br>I don't have a problem with a wimpy main character... just when they are THIS hypocritical (and boring) it gets old. Fast. <br><br>So Lark says things like this:<blockquote>
  <i>I didn’t want to be taken care of. I wanted to run away from all the men who sought dominion over me, who thought they could own me, imprison me, use me, cut me.</i>
</blockquote>Constantly, but all she does is actions like this: <blockquote>
  <i>f I didn’t breathe too deeply, I wouldn’t feel the hollow echo in my empty chest.</i>
</blockquote>And this: <blockquote>
  <i> If I didn’t move too quickly, I wouldn’t reach any painful conclusions.</i>
</blockquote>AND THIS:<blockquote>
  <i>...if I didn’t listen, I wouldn’t hear the silence he always left behind.</i>
</blockquote> Aka, she has <b>the backbone of a jellyfish </b>and spends the entire book hanging out in a castle, drawing words on the furniture with the king. <br><br>For a book that has<b> so much potential,</b> it was disappointingly BORING because the wimpy main character spent more time whining about what she hasn't done instead of actually DOING THINGS. <br><br>To be fair, I suppose she left her rooms like twice... so that's something. <br><br><b>
  <u>The Love Interest - <i>aka nothing says I love you like ruining your life...</i></u>
</b> <br><br>Lark is captured by King Trias within the first 50 pages and that's when the story really began to go downhill. <br><br>We go from this <b>intriguing, magical world</b> and then it becomes Lark hiding in a castle, Lark learning how to read, Lark "falling in love" with the King while they write words on her furniture. <br><br>The whole "falling in love" schtick was chock full of unquestionably awful quotes. <blockquote>
  <i>‘‘You were not supposed to love me, Lark. I did not set out to make you love me. And I was not supposed to love you. But I do. And it is terrible.’’</i>
</blockquote> <b>Are you serious? </b>Terrible? That's the best you can do for your confession? <br><br>It's like, I get that their love is supposed to be forbidden, that the King falling in love with a teller is the ultimate betrayal...<b>
  <i>but couldn't the author at least try to make it appealing?</i>
</b><br><br>I don't mind romance being a cruel-to-kindness sort of transformation, but that kindness is key. To see that transformation and believe it...<br><br>The main characters have to click together, and that just never happened. There was far too much <b>anguish and angst. </b><blockquote>
  <i>You chose me because I am of use. But I chose you because I wanted you. All I ever wanted was for you to love me in return. </i>
</blockquote> Talk about romance. There's even a line like this: <blockquote>
  <i>‘‘Because you just said you know nothing about being a queen. Because I am king. And because it is your duty to please me.’’</i>
</blockquote>And this:<blockquote>
  <i>‘‘You are a great use to me. I will put a child in your belly. A son who will be king.’’</i>
</blockquote> So, <b>I was just not feeling it..</b>.and 3/4 of the content was spent on building this mess of a relationship.<br><br><b>
  <u>Overall</u>
</b><br><br>If Lark was just cut from this book and the romance dropped, I would have loved it.<br><br> Such a well-written novel, lovely twist on magic and truly a memorable cast...just Lark was there in the middle, ruining everything forever.<br><br><a href="http://bit.ly/33ii2CT" rel="nofollow noopener">YouTube</a> | <a href="http://www.mirandareads.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/miranda.reads/?hl=en" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/Miranda_Reads" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | Snapchat @miranda.reads <br><br>Happy Reading!</span>
  <a data-text-id="10803924682670728992" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<div id="review_1650775604" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1650775604" />
    <a title="Cristina Monica" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica"><img alt="Cristina Monica" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1589617514p2/14596170.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1650775604?book_show_action=true">May 27, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cristina Monica" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cristina Monica" href="/user/show/14596170-cristina-monica">Cristina Monica</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magical-creatures">magical-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14596170-cristina-monica?shelf=magic">magic</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1650775604" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13276858524859509830">The writing is truly enchanting:<br/><br/><blockquote> <em>‘‘Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them ‘til they’ve time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, ‘til the hour. You won’t speak and you won’t tell, you won’t call on heav’n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, daughter. Stay alive.’’</em></blockquote><br/><em> </em>But sadly, that is the only element The Bird and the Sword is memorable for.<br/><br/>When I began my reading of it, I was sure </span>
  <span id="freeText13276858524859509830" style="display:none">The writing is truly enchanting:<br /><br /><blockquote> <em>‘‘Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them ‘til they’ve time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, ‘til the hour. You won’t speak and you won’t tell, you won’t call on heav’n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, daughter. Stay alive.’’</em></blockquote><br /><em> </em>But sadly, that is the only element The Bird and the Sword is memorable for.<br /><br />When I began my reading of it, I was sure I would end up giving it a five-star rating. The first chapters introduce the reader to the fantasy world created by Amy Harmon. We learn of the magic and discover the various magical creatures and abilities within the world-building.<br /><br />It is quite compelling. Until it isn’t anymore.<br /><br />The beautiful, intriguing storytelling does not last. From the moment Trias, the King, captures Lark, the story slowly starts to lose its appeal.<br /><br />For one, the love interest is anything but romantic. His idea of romance is not one usually welcome in fantasy reads. I personally prefer my fantasy love interests to be charming, have a sense of humor and hold deep respect for the heroine.<br /><br />Trias is the King and <strong>he knows it. </strong>Here are a couple of quotes of his that made me cringe:<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <em>Why do I have to be taught?<br />‘‘Because you just said you know nothing about being a queen. Because I am king. And because it is your duty to please me.’’</em>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>...</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <em> ‘‘You are a great use to me. I will put a child in your belly. A son who will be king.’’</em>
</blockquote><br /><blockquote>...</blockquote><br /><blockquote>
  <em>‘‘You were not supposed to love me, Lark. I did not set out to make you love me. And I was not supposed to love you. But I do. And it is terrible.’’</em>
</blockquote><br /><br /><em> </em><strong>Any man who will ever dare utter such abominable words to my face will lose an arm. </strong><br /><br /><strong> </strong>So the romance does not even deserve half a star.<br /><br />The story, however, is much better than the characters. There is very little happening – more telling than showing – but thanks to the formidable writing, it was not a bother to read it. I strongly suggest Amy Harmon reads more fantasy novels in her future because those are supposed to contain adventure and action and magic and The Bird and the Sword gives the feeling that it was written by a beginner in the genre.<br /><br />Countless repetitions and many, many missed opportunities.<br /><br />Like I said, the only memorable thing about it is the writing. Very beautiful indeed. But that is all.<br /><br />PS. Not only does Trias not know how to speak to a woman, but he has no idea how to apostrophe one either. No, saying ‘‘you stubborn woman,’’ is not the best way to win a woman’s heart. Really, Lark, what were you thinking?<br /><br /><a href="https://hitormissbooks.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.youtube.com/c/LolaReviewer" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a>Twitter</a> | <a>Instagram</a> | <a href="https://plus.google.com/u/0/105021852309973899120/posts" rel="nofollow noopener">Google+</a> | <a href="https://www.bloglovin.com/blogs/hit-miss-books-12564715" rel="nofollow noopener">Bloglovin’</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="13276858524859509830" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1720491442" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1720491442" />
    <a title="Katerina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina"><img alt="Katerina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1470667070p2/5014021.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1720491442?book_show_action=true">Dec 26, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Katerina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Katerina" href="/user/show/5014021-katerina">Katerina</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5014021-katerina?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1720491442" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9352857968934477928"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You don't need wings to fly.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>What you truly need is <b>words</b>. And <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon' title='Amy Harmon' rel='nofollow noopener'>Amy Harmon</a>'s words resulted in a work of <b>sheer beauty</b>, that made your chest clench with <b>yearning</b> and your entire existence float, leaving behind every material attachment and concern.<br/><a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29008738.The_Bird_and_the_Sword' title='The Bird and the Sword by Amy Harmon' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bird and the Sword</a> was a <b>piece of a dream</b>.<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482763000ra/21546855.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/> <br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Silence daughter, stay alive.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/>Once upon a time, the Gifted walked freely in the country of Jeru. Healers, Tellers, Spinners, Changers, they were not afraid of using their gods-besto</span>
  <span id="freeText9352857968934477928" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You don't need wings to fly.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>What you truly need is <b>words</b>. And <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a>'s words resulted in a work of <b>sheer beauty</b>, that made your chest clench with <b>yearning</b> and your entire existence float, leaving behind every material attachment and concern.<br><a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29008738.The_Bird_and_the_Sword" title="The Bird and the Sword by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bird and the Sword</a> was a <b>piece of a dream</b>.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482763000ra/21546855.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Silence daughter, stay alive.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Once upon a time, the Gifted walked freely in the country of Jeru. Healers, Tellers, Spinners, Changers, they were not afraid of using their gods-bestowed gifts. But some of them used them for Evil. And thus, the Gifted were hunted. They hid their abilities, or suffered terrible punishment. Lark's mother was not lucky. She was murdered for a crime she didn't even committ, and when her soul left her body, so did Lark's voice. Her father protected her out of necessity, but she was mostly ignored and left alone. Until Tiras, the king who fought desperately against the nightmarish creatures that threatened his kingdom and his people, decided to use her as a pawn. But she became more. <i>They</i> became more. And Lark, the silent girl with the power of words, the Bird, the Sword, would be the one to determine the outcome of the bloody war.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Daughter, daughter, Jeru's daughter,<br>Wait for him, his heart is true.<br>Daughter, daughter, Jeru's daughter,<br>'Til the hour he comes for you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>When I read books like <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29008738.The_Bird_and_the_Sword" title="The Bird and the Sword by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bird and the Sword</a>, I feel humble. Like I just bore witness to the most genuine form of <b>magic</b>, a golden thread of magic that was woven around my soul and captured it. There was something <b>otherworldly</b> in <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a>'s <b>simple</b> yet <b>eloquent, lyrical</b> writing. A fairytale that was narrated for me and only me, whispered by a soft, soothing voice. Her words, her sentences, they filled my veins and warmed my heart. It was a <b>beautiful</b> experience.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I have all the power, but you will destroy me.” </i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Politics. Magic. War. Powerful, devastating love</b>. That's what <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29008738.The_Bird_and_the_Sword" title="The Bird and the Sword by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bird and the Sword</a> masterly delivers. The world-building is not particularly complex, because the story focuses on Lark's journey to find her voice, her magic and her place in the world. From the girl that was always ignored, she becomes a powerful, strong woman willing to fight for what she wants, to break the chains that hold her down and <i>fly</i>. To a better future. To a brighter future. To <i>her</i> future. And her companion is none other than the captivating, infuriating and stubborn king, with his secrets and his struggles, a king who wants to tame the beast and let the Man prevail.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You said I choose you because you are of use to me. And I did. But know this, Lark. I have loved you every moment of every day, and I will love you until I cease to be. Bird, man, or king, I love you, and I will always love you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>There is passion and tenderness, fights and understanding in the relationship between Tiras and Lark. Their connection, the way their souls are in sync, makes your eyes water and your blood sing. Breathless and mesmerized, you watch them falling and you can't help but fall yourself. Fall, dream, hope, mourn, worry. Love. Love <i>them</i>, <i>with them</i>.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“A bird cannot wield a sword.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But a bird can <i>be</i> a sword. And Lark was both. <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a>'s soulful and poetic writing spoke to me, and I beg you to give her a chance to speak to you as well. She deserves it.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1482763000ra/21546856.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="9352857968934477928" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1542967164?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christy" href="/user/show/11284813-christy">Christy</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1542967164" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17173330825978149368"><b>5 stars!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/DA9E9EFE-E9F4-4C13-8324-8F3E0216EE38_zps72xwcnza.jpg.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463055272i/19077338._SY540_.jpg' alt=' photo DA9E9EFE-E9F4-4C13-8324-8F3E0216EE38_zps72xwcnza.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/>I only read fantasy occasionally, so this isn’t a book I would normally pick up right away... BUT Amy Harmon is one of my favorite authors so I knew I would read it as soon as I got the chance. I’m so glad I did. <i>The Bird and the Sword</i> is a story that sucked me in from the start. A completely captivating read with equal parts romance and adventure. <br/><br/>Amy’s writing and story telling abilities is nothing short of magical here. If this book has any message at all, it’s that words are powe</span>
  <span id="freeText17173330825978149368" style="display:none"><b>5 stars!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/DA9E9EFE-E9F4-4C13-8324-8F3E0216EE38_zps72xwcnza.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463055272i/19077338._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo DA9E9EFE-E9F4-4C13-8324-8F3E0216EE38_zps72xwcnza.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>I only read fantasy occasionally, so this isn’t a book I would normally pick up right away... BUT Amy Harmon is one of my favorite authors so I knew I would read it as soon as I got the chance. I’m so glad I did. <i>The Bird and the Sword</i> is a story that sucked me in from the start. A completely captivating read with equal parts romance and adventure. <br><br>Amy’s writing and story telling abilities is nothing short of magical here. If this book has any message at all, it’s that words are powerful. Coming from this author, it’s a very apt message. In all her books, her words are moving, brilliant and powerful. This book is no exception. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/50F8366C-C551-46C4-B6DF-F40DFD0A9E0E_zpsxxjbqq4n.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463055272i/19077339._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 50F8366C-C551-46C4-B6DF-F40DFD0A9E0E_zpsxxjbqq4n.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><i>The Bird and the Sword</i> is full of heart, magic, beauty, adventure and love. The characters are so lovable. I loved Lark’s voice and her story. At first, I didn’t think this was going to be a love story. I didn’t see how a romance would be possible at the start, but I was happy to be proven wrong. If you need a little romance in your books like me, you’ll be happy to know that the love in this book is strong. <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/839337C6-A2B0-4BB7-8036-2C0897782949_zps9ebn5hg2.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463055373i/19077356._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 839337C6-A2B0-4BB7-8036-2C0897782949_zps9ebn5hg2.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Without any spoilers, it’s hard to go into the plot of this story and what it’s about, so I won’t. Just know that it’s a phenomenal book with brilliant writing and going on my must-read list! Fantasy lovers and romance lovers alike should give this book a go! Once again, Amy Harmon does not disappoint with her poignant words and beautiful, original story lines. <i>The Bird and the Sword</i> gets a full 5 stars from me! <br><br><a href="http://s1279.photobucket.com/user/Christyb23/media/Book%20Reviews%209/650B53E5-D0A4-4264-8C2A-AED1F734AE56_zpsf1q0qtmw.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463055272i/19077340._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 650B53E5-D0A4-4264-8C2A-AED1F734AE56_zpsf1q0qtmw.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a></span>

<div id="review_1635732872" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1635732872" />
    <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog"><img alt="Aestas Book Blog" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1353371225p2/5604583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1635732872?book_show_action=true">May 11, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Aestas Book Blog" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Aestas Book Blog" href="/user/show/5604583-aestas-book-blog">Aestas Book Blog</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5604583-aestas-book-blog?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1635732872" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4254184563924900968"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: </b><br/><img width='100%' src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463167040i/19089414.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>Silence, daughter. Stay alive."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br/><strong>WOW!! What an enchanting story! This book was beautifully written, stunningly imaginative, poetic, thrilling, romantic, and exciting. Reading it was like going on an adventure and being swept away in a fantastical fairy tale filled with danger, magic, and woven together with a love story! I’ve loved this author’s writing for a long time and this story was exceptional!! If you’re looking for new book to read that is captiv</strong></span>
  <span id="freeText4254184563924900968" style="display:none"><b> ::: FULL REVIEW NOW POSTED ::: </b><br><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463167040i/19089414.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <em>
    <strong>Silence, daughter. Stay alive."</strong>
  </em>
</blockquote><br><strong>WOW!! What an enchanting story! This book was beautifully written, stunningly imaginative, poetic, thrilling, romantic, and exciting. Reading it was like going on an adventure and being swept away in a fantastical fairy tale filled with danger, magic, and woven together with a love story! I’ve loved this author’s writing for a long time and this story was exceptional!! If you’re looking for new book to read that is captivating and unique, definitely try this!</strong><br><br>I'm sure you can guess from reading the blurb, but you should know for sure that this is a Fantasy Romance novel -- we're talking kings, queens, and kingdoms in peril, not to mention magic and monsters -- which is totally different than the Contemporary Romance novels I usually read. But the kinds of stories that captivate me the most are the ones that step outside the lines while still staying true to the elements I love and crave from the Romance genre. Amy Harmon's writing is some of the very best I've ever read so when I heard she'd written a Fantasy novel, I honestly didn't even need to see the blurb to know I wanted to read it. And I was truly impressed with how seamlessly she slipped from the Contemporary genre into this sweeping Fantasy epic that I now consider a favorite.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"In a land purged of enchantment, love might be the only magic left."</em>
</blockquote><br>The story takes place in another world, somewhat similar to our Middle Ages in feeling. In this world, many are Gifted and Words have power and, if used correctly, a Word may come to life and manifest as true actions. But such powers are feared and forbidden and as such anyone with them must keep them hidden in order to survive...<br><br><blockquote>
  <em><strong>"Swallow, daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them ‘til they’ve time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, ‘til the hour. You won’t speak and you won’t tell, you won’t call on heaven or hell. You will learn and you will thrive.<br>Silence, daughter. Stay alive."</strong><br><br>The day my mother was killed, she told my father I wouldn’t speak again, and she told him if I died, he would die too. Then she predicted the king would sell his soul and lose his son to the sky.<br><br>My father has a claim to the throne, and he is waiting in the shadows for all of my mother’s words to come to pass. He wants desperately to be king, and I just want to be free.<br><br>But freedom will require escape, and I’m a prisoner of my mother’s curse and my father’s greed. I can’t speak or make a sound, and I can’t wield a sword or beguile a king. In a land purged of enchantment, love might be the only magic left, and who could ever love... a bird?</em>
</blockquote><br>I really don't want to give too much away but just to give you an idea of the story. The heroine has powers that even she doesn't really understand but that you see develop over the course of the book. The young king, who remembers her from the fateful day they met as children, captures her and brings her back to his kingdom where their story truly begins. His intent for her capture was at first political, but as they spent more time together, an unexpected love began to grow between them...<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>“I think I will keep you.”</em>
</blockquote><br>This is truly a Fantasy novel so if you're intrigued, be prepared to be swept away into a world of wars, love, and magic. I found myself completely enthralled by this story. I lost track of time while reading it and barely noticed the hours ticking away. It was such a wonderful experience to read a book so different than my norm.<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>‘I am not a weapon. I don’t want to be a weapon!’<br>“You are what you are. I am what I am. It matters little what we want… I never wanted to be king. But it is what I am. It matters little what we want,” he repeated. I turned and stared up into his face, filled with an anguish that wouldn’t abate.<br>‘You’re wrong. It is the thing that matters most.’<br>“Why?” he murmured, his eyes intent.<br>‘Because without desire, there is only duty.”</em>
</blockquote><br>Given that I am a true Romance reader at heart and often have a hard time stepping too far outside of my preferred genre, I was pleasantly surprised to see that this was a Fantasy novel that completely stayed true to the rules of Romance. I loved that the story was always developing and constantly moving forward, keeping me eager to read more and find out what path their journey would take them down next. It was a thrilling adventure that culminated in an epic battle that I could easily see playing out in my head like a movie.<br><br>The love story is quite beautifully woven into the story. It's quite poetic and the epilogue's final words brought happy tears to my eyes as it truly brought the story full circle. It was a beautiful ending for a beautiful book!<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>"You were not supposed to love me. I did not set out to make you love me. And I was not supposed to love you. But... I have loved you every moment of every day, and I will love you until I cease to be. Bird, man, or king, I love you, and I will always love you.”</em>
</blockquote><br>I can't say enough good things about Amy Harmon's writing. She is such a gifted storyteller and her books are one-of-a-kind gems. If you're new to her books, I highly recommend checking out <a href="http://amzn.to/1rIA6Dg" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Faces</a> (a contemporary novel) as well as this one because I consider it to be one of the best books I've ever read... and if you're either already a fantasy fan or if you're looking for something unique, different, and amazing, then I highly recommend <a href="http://amzn.to/24Tw909" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">this book</a>.<br><blockquote>
  <em>“Wait for him,” she pressed, and there was an urgency that belied her simple advice…<br>‘For how long?’<br>“As long as it takes.”</em>
</blockquote><br><strong>Rating: 4.5 stars! Standalone Fantasy (Romance) novel.<br>But... the writing itself is 5 stars all the way!</strong><br> <br> 	 <strong><a href="http://amzn.to/24Tw909" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Buy THE BIRD AND THE SWORD (Kindle)</a></strong> <br> 	 <a href="http://amzn.to/1sj7ilp" rel="nofollow noopener"><strong>Buy THE BIRD AND THE SWORD (Paperback)</strong></a> <br> <br>__________________________<br><br><b> For more of my reviews, book news and updates:<br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener">Main blog: Aestas Book Blog</a><br>✦ <a href="http://www.facebook.com/pages/Aestas-Book-Blog/332404836826905" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook Blog Page</a><br>✦ <a href="https://twitter.com/AestasBookBlog" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> <br>✦ <a href="http://aestasbookblog.com/subscribe/" rel="nofollow noopener">Subscribe by email</a> <br><br><a href="http://aestasbookblog.com" rel="nofollow noopener"><img width="100%" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380306821i/688100._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a> </b></span>

    <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake"><img alt="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1605987751p2/11626803.jpg" /></a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️" href="/user/show/11626803-val-shameless-non-snowflake">Val ⚓️ Shameless Non-Snowflake ⚓️</a>

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

  <span id="freeText3874658094627584683" style="display:none"><b>4 Stars</b><br><br>I originally rated this book 4 stars with "3.75 Stars" written in the text box here. <br><br>And then I realized that was fucking stupid. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1490132473ra/22284639.gif" width="480" height="270" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>So, 4 big ones, peeps.<br><br>But moving on. <br><br>I love it when I crack open a book - Well, to be fair, I'm not really "crackin' open anything...more like lightly finger tapping; however, "I love it when I lightly finger tap open a book" just doesn't have the same flair, holla?<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455867903ra/18160135.gif" width="500" height="250" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Anywordsmithing.<br><br>I love it when I crack open a book and see a map. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495656443i/22842457._SY540_.jpg" width="282" height="376" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Because that usually means that I'm about to enter a fantastical world of make believe as created solely by the author. <br><br>And if that map is followed by a pronunciation guide?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1495656443i/22842458._SY540_.jpg" width="282" height="376" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Fucking <i>sweet</i>. <br><br>Because that usually means...that we are about to enter a fantastical world of make believe as created solely by the author. <br><br>And that I don't have to fumble fuck around trying to imagine how to pronounce shit and spend the whole book trying to make "Tiras" happen. <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1495656929ra/22842587.gif" width="500" height="278" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>That said, the world building in this book was fantastic.<br><br>I love kingdom books. <br><br>And not only was this a kingdom book, it was a <i>paranormal</i> kingdom book where people have magic powers. <br><br>Magic powers, people.<br><br>Instant orgasm. <br> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1429106079ra/14530408.gif" width="379" height="287" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Lark was my favorite kind of heroine: understated and low key with a spine of steel. <br><br>Tiras' character was also very interesting. Throughout the book I enjoyed his interactions and I enjoyed his bond with Kjell as much - if not more than - his growing bond with Lark. <br><br>So why not 5 stars, you ask?<br><br>The ending action felt a little rough to me as far as the way it all went down and the way it was written. <br><br>Other than that, I adored this thing and have already downloaded the next book in the series. <br><br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_1996741672" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1996741672" />
    <a title="Melanie" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie"><img alt="Melanie" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1577914102p2/3030788.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1996741672?book_show_action=true">May 21, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melanie" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melanie" href="/user/show/3030788-melanie">Melanie</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



          <div>
    <span class="greyText">Recommended to Melanie by: </span>
      <a href="/user/show/7345713-paloma-the-romance-queen">Paloma *The Romance Queen* </a>
  </div>


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=shifters">shifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=new-adult">new-adult</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3030788-melanie?shelf=read-in-2017">read-in-2017</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1996741672" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7241390397287782198"><i>The Bird and the Sword</i> had such an unexpectedly beautiful prose, with such lyrical writing. I was completely swept away by how whimsically this tale was told. Amy Harmon has such talent, and I went into this expecting nothing, but I ending up being blown away by this fantasy novel. Seriously, this is not hyped nearly enough. <br/><br/>Also, on a completely personal side note, this book's main protagonist has an abbreviated version of my favorite name of all time, Larkin. So, besides the enthralling writin</span>
  <span id="freeText7241390397287782198" style="display:none"><i>The Bird and the Sword</i> had such an unexpectedly beautiful prose, with such lyrical writing. I was completely swept away by how whimsically this tale was told. Amy Harmon has such talent, and I went into this expecting nothing, but I ending up being blown away by this fantasy novel. Seriously, this is not hyped nearly enough. <br /><br />Also, on a completely personal side note, this book's main protagonist has an abbreviated version of my favorite name of all time, Larkin. So, besides the enthralling writing, I was completely fangirling over the use of the name Lark, too, because I've never read a story using it before. <br /><br />Okay, so this book starts out with Lark being very young and still learning the dangers of her magical gift. In this world, Gifted people are sentenced to death, so it is very imperative to hide your magical powers if you are born with any. <br /><br /><b>
  <u>The Four Types of Gifted Magic:</u>
</b><br />➽ <b><u>Spinners</u> -</b> Have the ability to turn things into other things. <br />➽ <b><u>Changers</u>-</b> Can shape shift into other animals.<br />➽ <b><u>Healers</u> -</b> Are able to heal bodies and cure wounds.<br />➽ <b><u>Tellers</u> -</b> Use magic words that compel people and things to do things. This magic is very much like casting spells, and very powerful. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“My mother made words. She was a Teller, and her words were magic. She spoke and the words became life. Reality. Truth. My father knew it, and he was afraid. Words can be terrible when the truth is unwelcome.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />Lark is a Teller like her mother, and her mother pays the ultimate price for her carelessness to hide her powers. Her mother is killed by the King of Jeru, but not before she tells the King, Lark's father, and Lark herself, a few prophetic things. Her mother's premonition-like rhymes also makes Lark lose her ability to speak. <br /><br />We are then thrust into the future, where our dear Lark is still unable to communicate besides head nods. She does have an amazing Troll companion named Boojohni that I completely fell in love with. They sort of form their own way to speak, and he has become Lark's only friend over the years. <br /><br />Then one day, while out in the forest, Lark stumbles upon a fatally injured bird. Even though she only has the voice inside in head, she tries to use her Teller powers to compel the bird's body into healing itself. The next thing she knows, she is waking up in the forest and then is running home because the new King is arriving to meet with her father. <br /><br />Lark's father, Corvyn, is a Lord and hasn't sent any men to help fight against the Volgar. The Volgar are winged evil monsters that are lead by the Volgar Liege. Their numbers are constantly growing, and they are taking over more and more land. The new King, Tiras, son of the old King that killed Lark's mother, captures Lark and plans to use her as hostage. Tiras tells Corvyn that he can have his daughter back, once he sends his share of men to help defeat the Volgar. <br /><br />And the story quickly, and very addictively, starts from there. <br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Suddenly yearning had a flavor. It tasted like a king, a beautiful, frightening, infuriating man who flew into my life and began to free my words.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br />The characters are so very wonderful, and Lark is such a strong female character that learns her worth and won't settle for less than what she deserves. The story is fast paced and full of intrigue and mystery, while proving over and over that words are the most powerful weapon we will ever truly wield. The magic system is easy to understand, but still really enchanting. The romance in this book is seriously top notch, and if you guys are anything like me and some of your favorite parts of <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1278845732" rel="nofollow noopener">A Court of Mist and Fury</a> were the ones where Feyre is taught to read, then you are going to freakin' love some of the scenes in this book. Seriously, be still, my heart, because I'm still not over how heartwarming and perfect those scenes were.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I have loved you every moment of every day, and I will love you until I cease to be.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br /><i>The Bird and the Sword</i> is the perfect mix of fantasy and romance. If you are like me, and enjoy both of those genres, then you have to pick this book up. I loved this and I absolutely cannot wait to read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2006772193?book_show_action=false" rel="nofollow noopener"> The Queen and the Cure</a>. <br /><br /><a href="https://www.youtube.com/channel/UC4RbHEg_fH6CewJrh_0xJ9g" rel="nofollow noopener">Youtube</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/meltotheany/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.twitter.com/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://meltotheany.wordpress.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://open.spotify.com/user/meltotheany?si=kHJ5JnLHQsSp23fDe0qxSQ" rel="nofollow noopener">Spotify</a> | <a href="http://www.twitch.tv/meltotheany" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitch</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="7241390397287782198" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1766424718" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1766424718" />
    <a title="Bibi" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi"><img alt="Bibi" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1602128191p2/33411728.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1766424718?book_show_action=true">Oct 20, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Bibi" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Bibi" href="/user/show/33411728-bibi">Bibi</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30171592-the-bird-and-the-sword">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1766424718" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4719534490563939716"><b>I'm so frigging happy right now, you can't even imagine!</b><br/><br/><a href='http://s1248.photobucket.com/user/bibifagboyegun/media/inyqrgp9o3NUA_zps9f5b944b.gif.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477019764ra/20907670.gif' alt=' photo inyqrgp9o3NUA_zps9f5b944b.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>I was instantly mesmerized by <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29008738-the-bird-and-the-sword' rel='nofollow noopener'>The Bird and the Sword</a>, a book that interweaves fantasy with heart-melting romance. The book opens in Corvyn, a province of the Land of Jeru, where we meet Lady Lark of Coryvn, daughter of Lord Corvyn and Lady Meshara, <b> a girl gifted with the power of words. This power is dangerous and it, being completely forbidden in this mythical land, must remain a secret.</b><br/><br/>For a book with numerous characters, we only get</span>
  <span id="freeText4719534490563939716" style="display:none"><b>I'm so frigging happy right now, you can't even imagine!</b><br><br><a href="http://s1248.photobucket.com/user/bibifagboyegun/media/inyqrgp9o3NUA_zps9f5b944b.gif.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1477019764ra/20907670.gif" alt=" photo inyqrgp9o3NUA_zps9f5b944b.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>I was instantly mesmerized by <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29008738-the-bird-and-the-sword" rel="nofollow noopener">The Bird and the Sword</a>, a book that interweaves fantasy with heart-melting romance. The book opens in Corvyn, a province of the Land of Jeru, where we meet Lady Lark of Coryvn, daughter of Lord Corvyn and Lady Meshara, <b> a girl gifted with the power of words. This power is dangerous and it, being completely forbidden in this mythical land, must remain a secret.</b><br><br>For a book with numerous characters, we only get 2 POVs; one is Lady Meshara and the other, Lark. <br>Meshara's POV sets off this story and is no more that 13 pages, but those pages are pivotal and they evoke all sorts of emotions; disbelief, anger, intrigue, and anticipation. I couldn't flick the e-reader fast enough. I was hooked.<br><br>King Zoltev of Degn and his son, King Tiras of Degn. Boojohni the troll. Kjell. Lady Firi. The Tellers. The Healers. The Changers. The Spinners. The Council members.<br><br><b>All are characters who play vital roles in this story.</b><br><br>Lark provides the 2nd POV for the remainder of this book, so it's important to mention that at some point- almost from the beginning of the book -she becomes mute. How do you tell a story when the narrator cannot speak? Sounds impossible, doesn't it? Yet Harmon navigates this aspect brilliantly. <br><br><b>Harmon moves the story along with impeccable pacing and suddenly Lark finds herself a pawn and a hostage in the hands of the young King Tiras of Degn, a king who has dark secrets of his own. Tiras's intentions are completely dishonorable with Lark being nothing but a means of keeping Lord Corvyn from overthrowing him as King.</b><br><br>Lark and Tiras soon find that a lot actually binds them together and they're are not so different from each other after all. Meanwhile, dissension from the council members brews, dark creatures close in wanting nothing more than to rip to pieces the Land of Jeru, and former allies turn treacherous. <br><br>With no one left to trust, Tiras and Lark find they must work together to conquer the evil forces and with such, their feelings evolve, trust superimposed with love blossoms, and fierce loyalty to each other makes them a formidable team. But with both of them having such damaging secrets, will their enemies prevail or will their love survive? <br><br><b>Harmon wrote with exquisite detail, and for over 6 hours I remained captivated and was completely transported to Jeru, where I could picture the beautiful landscape with its diverse creatures, feel the pulsating oppression of evil and, with the last 25% being so action-packed and nerve wracking, I was perpetually on the edge of my seat, not wanting the story to end! <br><br>There's so much more that I can tell you about this story, so much more. But I have no intention of spoiling it; as it is, I feel I may have divulged too much still I'm confident that I barely scratched the surface. <br><br>It was amazing, entertaining and brilliant!</b></span>
  <a data-text-id="4719534490563939716" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div id="review_1715359134" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1715359134" />
    <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow"><img alt="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1393785730p2/10336538.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1715359134?book_show_action=true">Aug 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ " href="/user/show/10336538-jessica-silverbow">Jessica ❁ ➳ Silverbow ➳ ❁ </a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30171592-the-bird-and-the-sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=convoluted-plans">convoluted-plans</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=buddy-reads-are-the-best">buddy-reads-are-the-best</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=riddikulus">riddikulus</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=what-the-hype">what-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=not-your-ordinary-creatures">not-your-ordinary-creatures</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=indie">indie</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=some-kinda-magic">some-kinda-magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=rabid-reads-reviews">rabid-reads-reviews</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/10336538-jessica-silverbow?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1715359134" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6578753162510383120"><b>Reviewed by: <a href='http://rabidreads.ca/2016/08/review-the-bird-and-the-sword-by-amy-harmon-jessicadhaluska.html' target='_blank' rel='nofollow noopener'>Rabid Reads</a></b><br/><br/>I have friends who are bargain hunters. They stalk the aisles of stores like T.J. Maxx and Marshalls, searching for last season frocks from Kate Spade and Lilly Pulitzer, and are often successful. They preen over their discoveries, and I sometimes envy the fruits of their labors . . . <br/><br/>BUT. I will never be able to do it myself. <br/><br/>Those types of places are too chaotic; I walk in the door and immediately turn and walk back out. B/c overwhelmed. There's so much stuff shoved tog</span>
  <span id="freeText6578753162510383120" style="display:none"><b>Reviewed by: <a href="http://rabidreads.ca/2016/08/review-the-bird-and-the-sword-by-amy-harmon-jessicadhaluska.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">Rabid Reads</a></b><br><br>I have friends who are bargain hunters. They stalk the aisles of stores like T.J. Maxx and Marshalls, searching for last season frocks from Kate Spade and Lilly Pulitzer, and are often successful. They preen over their discoveries, and I sometimes envy the fruits of their labors . . . <br><br>BUT. I will never be able to do it myself. <br><br>Those types of places are too chaotic; I walk in the door and immediately turn and walk back out. B/c overwhelmed. There's so much stuff shoved together so haphazardly that I haven't the foggiest notion of where to begin. <br><br>THE BIRD AND THE SWORD had a similar effect, and I'm kind of baffled that the same author who wrote <b>
  <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/29698573-a-different-blue" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">A Different Blue</a>
</b>, which I loved, also wrote something as poorly planned and executed as this was . . . But here we are.<br><br><b>MINOR SPOILERS after this point.</b><br><br><b>1. The journey is merely the shortest distance from point A to point B.</b><br><br>There are two main types of writers: those who plan and those who write by the seat of their pants, and if I had to guess, I'd venture that Harmon is the former.<br><br><b>You:</b> What makes you say that?<br><br><b>Me:</b> The extraordinarily stupid actions that enabled obvious plot points.<br><br>Take Lark's first adult encounter with King.<br><br>The last time they met was the day King's father (former King) killed her mother, b/c magic is outlawed. Having magic herself, Lark is understandably afraid when she belatedly learns that King will be visiting her home that very day. <br><br>So what does she do?<br><br>She tears off through the forest, determined to be hidden in a tower before King arrives, but when she hears horses pounding down the road, does she retreat back into the relative safety of woods? Does she hide herself until the riders have passed, slinking home behind them and avoiding detection?<br><br>NOPE.<br><br>She runs faster. <br><br>
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1471607349ra/20078795.gif" width="320" height="240" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>And that's just the beginning. <br><br><b>You:</b> What do you mean?<br><br><b>Me:</b> Father wants to usurp King. Has been planning it since the death of his wife.<br><br>So what does he do?<br><br>Lay low, scheming and machinating until the time is ripe for a coup?<br><br>NOPE.<br><br>He refuses the command to send soldiers to the war front, painting an arrow over his head that shouts, "MALCONTENT."<br><br><b>You:</b> That's not very smart . . . <br><br><b>Me:</b> Yeah, but, see, King needs to be able to take Lark hostage b/c reasons.<br><br><b>You:</b> Seems like kind of a bullshit way to make it happen though. <br><br><b>Me:</b> YES. It DOES.<br><br><b>2. Deliberately obtuse heroine.</b><br><br>The problem with telling a story from the first person perspective is that the reader gets ALL of her information directly from the source. SO. If a thing is more-than-obvious to the reader, it's incomprehensible if it isn't also more-than-obvious to the storyteller. <br><br>And yet . . . <br><br>*sing songs* <i>"My mother foretold that the former king would lose his son, the prince, 'to the skies . . .' The injured eagle I found in the forest disappeared while I slept, and I returned home to discover that one of my servants had been conked and the head and relieved of his clothes, and a horse was missing from the stables . . . King chained himself in the dungeon, tormented by a mysterious malady . . . Oh, look! It's my friend the eagle sitting on the rail of King's open balcony! Hello, friend eagle! Where ever could King be? He never returned last night . . ."</i> *blinks vapidly*<br><br><b>3. Conflicting information.</b><br><br>The following screenshot serves a variety of purposes, but for now, let's focus on the blue passage:<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472032975i/20140523.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>They are creatures, animals, ruled by instinct. They are PREDATORS. Like a shark scenting blood in the water or a bear whose normal food sources have been unnaturally depleted. <br><br>BUT.<br><br>If this is true, they cannot also be "base."<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1471604232i/20077842.jpg" width="300" height="360" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>To be "base" requires sentience, yet Harmon uses the mutually exclusive concepts of being governed by basic needs--food, water, shelter--and more nefarious or "base" motivations interchangeably. <br><br>My knee-jerk reaction was that she was confused about the meanings of "base" and "basic," but on the very next page:<br><br><blockquote>
  <em><strong>They lived to kill. Not for hate or power. But still, they killed. They killed because death meant food. Death meant life.</strong> Death meant that their blood pounded hotter in their veins, and their flesh grew thicker on their bones. They were simple monsters, but monsters all the same.</em>
</blockquote><br>And a paragraph or so further down, the earlier accusation is even more blatantly contradicted when she references the creature's, <em>"innocent instinct, however bloodthirsty."</em><br><br>So it's not that she doesn't understand the terms and the difference between them, it's that she was so concerned with finding flowery ways to present information that she either didn't care or didn't notice that the end result made not one lick of sense, which segues perfectly into my next issue . . . <br><br><b>4. Purple prose.</b><br><br>This time let's check out the yellow highlights:<br><br>
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472032975i/20140523.jpg" width="400" height="300" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
<br><br>Taken individually, all the various flourishes and embellishments might not be a problem. I mean, just b/c I've never personally experienced an "obliterated" appetite, and could come up with half a dozen less vague ways of describing the weather than "advantageous," doesn't mean that an emphatic adjective/adverb (or three) is a distraction.<br><br>BUT. As you can see, there are four on this page alone, and friends . . . that is not a fluke. <br><br>Then there's this:<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>Suddenly freed and temporarily weightless, the ground rose up and snatched my breath. I lay stunned, the wind forced from my lungs.</em>
</blockquote><br>The ground . . . rose up . . . and snatched her breath . . . *flares nostrils*<br><br><a href="https://www.pinterest.com/pin/134896951314579251/" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1472032975i/20140524.jpg" alt="I'm so fancy" width="300" height="196" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>NO. It did NOT. She fell and had the wind knocked out of her. The end. <br><br><b>5. There are just some things you CANNOT do.</b><br><br>Like reference real world works of literature in a wholly make-believe world:<br><br><blockquote>
  <i>"The Art of War?"</i>
</blockquote><br>BUT. That specific reference is borderline hilarious, b/c later on, King is so determined to engage the enemy on his terms that:<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>We rested a full day, giving the horses a chance to recuperate from the journey, but the collective unease of the camp made the day feel wasted. <strong>Shrieks and shouts filled the night as the Volgar picked off men in the dark</strong> . . .</em>
</blockquote><br>Huh. So the same King who is familiar enough with Sun Tzu's ART OF WAR to make jokes about the bloodthirsty discussion points, passively allows his soldiers to be attacked by their enemy?<br><br>I guess he skipped this part:<br><br><blockquote>
  <em>Regard your soldiers as your children, and they will follow you into the deepest valleys; look on them as your own beloved sons, and they will stand by you even unto death.</em>
</blockquote><br>And I'm done. DONE. D O N E. <br><br>Basically, I spent twice as much time deciphering the events and characters’ actions as I did reading this book. Whatever it is that the rest of the world sees in THE BIRD AND THE SWORD, I am immune, wholly and utterly. Not recommended. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1421060968i/13316940.jpg" alt="Jessica Signature" width="205" height="101" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="6578753162510383120" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2832712671" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer13680098685565099958">this book is magical enchantment at its finest. <br/><br/>the prose is a charming spell, all on its own - one that could lull me into the most peaceful of sleeps. <br/><br/>but the story itself is in a whole other league - its faithful to the traditions of old fairy tales but has a modern feel that is leaving me wishing for more. <br/><br/>it is sheer storytelling perfection. <br/><br/>i seriously cant get over how enamoured i am with this book. i am so in awe.<br/><br/><b>↠ <i>5 stars</i></b></span>

          </span>
