<div id="review_2594485017" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2594485017" />
    <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin"><img alt="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1603831478p2/17438949.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2594485017?book_show_action=true">Nov 14, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin" href="/user/show/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin">Melissa ♥ Dog/Wolf Lover ♥ Martin</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=kindle-own">kindle-own</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/17438949-melissa-dog-wolf-lover-martin?shelf=fantasy-all">fantasy-all</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2594485017" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6260677365126861328"><b>
  <blockquote>"Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them 'til they've time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, 'til the hour. You won't speak and you won't tell, you won't call on heav'n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, daughter. Stay alive."</blockquote>
</b><br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537840254ra/26349833.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>
  <blockquote>My mother made words. She was a Teller, and her words were magic. She spoke and the words became life. Reality. Truth. My father knew it, and he wa</blockquote></b></span>
  <span id="freeText6260677365126861328" style="display:none"><b>
  <blockquote>"Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them 'til they've time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, 'til the hour. You won't speak and you won't tell, you won't call on heav'n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, daughter. Stay alive."</blockquote>
</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537840254ra/26349833.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>
  <blockquote>My mother made words. She was a Teller, and her words were magic. She spoke and the words became life. Reality. Truth. My father knew it, and he was afraid. Words can be terrible when the truth is unwelcome.</blockquote>
</b><br><br>Omg!! This book was so freaking good! I mean holy sh•t snacks! I have had this book on my kindle FOREVER and finally read it! This book is magical! Seriously, there are a lot of magical beings in the book. <br><br>Healers <br>Shifters <br>Tellers . . . etc. There are many different Guifted people. But a lot of people want them all killed! <br><br>Larks mom tried to save her by taking her voice from her as a child. She wanted her to be safe. <br><br>Lark as a woman meets the love of her life. He teaches her to read in their own special way. He can hear her thoughts. Can Lark and this man change the rules and make things better. Can a man who is an Eagle save Lark as she saved him? <br><br>Read it and see! <br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1542232834ra/26598608.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Happy Reading!! <br><br>Mel 🖤🐶🐺🐾</span>

  <span id="freeText1649056709209265248" style="display:none">BUCKLE YOUR SEATBELTS, I JUST READ A GREAT BOOK SO GET READY FOR MY <b>REDBULL-INDUCED-MIND-BLOWN-WRITING-EXTRAVAGANZA!!</b> <br><br>Meet the crew: <br><b>Lark:</b> a very reSILENT character (im so awful).<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494548156ra/22727607.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> <br><br>In a world that fears all magic, Lark's mother places a curse that <b>
  <u>prevents her from magical voice from speaking</u>
</b>. Unable to voice her thoughts, she had an inner strength so unlike most heroines. Often heroines are loud and reckless. Lark was the opposite! <br><br>She understood words on a deeper level. While listening to Boo scolding her, she heard love. When hearing the concern of a lord of lady, she heard greed. <br>She reviewed each action <u>because for her actions spoke louder than words</u><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494548156ra/22727608.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I can’t make words. I can’t make a sound. I have thoughts and feelings. I have pictures and colors. They are all bottled up inside of me because I can’t make words.<br>But I can hear them.<br>The world is alive with words. The animals, the trees, the grass, and the birds hum with their own words. “Life,” they say.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><b>Boojohni:</b> comedic side character who I loved to read about and advanced the plot. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“He shuddered in horror. He seemed momentarily lost in the horrified speculation of his possible beardlessness”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494548156ra/22727609.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><u>With possibly the greatest name ever</u>, he was also a troll and deeply loyal to protecting Lark. Throughout the book, they work together and got amazing <br><br><b>Tiras:</b> snarky King without the usual arrogance, he was all to aware of his faults. <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“Without desire, there is only duty,” Tiras whispered, quoting me as I quoted him. “But sometimes our greatest desire is to do our duty.” Then he closed his eyes, as if offering up a prayer for strength, though I heard only his yearning, and it made my heart tremble.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>He was a king who made mistakes but really wanted to be fair and protect his kingdom. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455389853ra/18096946.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>And the plot twist... <br><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[HOLY CRAP THAT WAS GREAT when we found out he was a shape-changer but there was an awkward paws....i hate myself <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br><br><b>Kjell:</b> Tiras's right hand man who hates Lark for her gift and inner conflict which plays a huge role later. <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1455907894ra/18167624.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>*warning Dad is an asshole, I wanted to smack him upside the head<br><br>(Quick tangent: I absolutely loved the prologue. Wonderful way to begin the book~ great balance of world-building, introducing key characters, with some anticipating foreshadowing )<br><br><u>The banter!</u> <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1441620804ra/16130318.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“NO.<br>“Yes.”<br>Lust is different from desire. There are women who will gladly assuage your lust. I will not.<br>“You want me. I heard it. I feel it.”<br>It matters little what we want, I shot back, using his words against him. I may be your weapon. But I am not your queen.<br>He sat back on his haunches, his hands on his thighs, and he considered me.<br>“Do you want to be my queen?”<br>Why would I want that?<br>“Most women would.”<br>I am not most women.<br>“You don’t want power? Riches?”<br>Power only gets you killed.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Life lessons here people! <br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I tried to instruct the soot to disappear too, but it stubbornly remained, proving that I could put out the fire, but I couldn’t yet save myself from the natural consequences of my mistakes.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>I loved how this book featured basic life lessons in new unexpected ways. Great balance of plot, character development and not just bloodshed bloodshed bloodshed<br><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“I wished I had let him kill me instead.”<br>Why?<br>“Because in that moment, as I watched him die, I felt something leave me too. Like he’d taken part of my soul. The best part. I’ve never gotten it back. And I miss it.”</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br>This book was honestly a delight to read with a character so unlike anything I've read before and such a great amazing of action without the usual BLOOD SHED BLOOD SHED VIOLENCE DEATH THE END <br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1494548156ra/22727610.gif" width="200" height="200" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer15622784285989781192">A girl without a voice. A king in chains. A land on the brink of war. <br/><br/>Intrigued? <br/><br/><b>YOU SHOULD BE. </b><br/><br/>Ever since I read <i>Radiance</i> last year, I’ve been on the lookout for more books in the Fantasy Romance subgenre. Which is why I picked this one up. <br/><br/>Only…<br/><br/>While it’s listed as a fantasy, it has all the trappings of a classic fairy tale. I mean that in the BEST possible way. There are curses, prophecies, evil sorcerers, gallant princes, reluctant princesses, and creatures of all shapes and sizes. <br/><br/>I absolut</span>
  <span id="freeText15622784285989781192" style="display:none">A girl without a voice. A king in chains. A land on the brink of war. <br /><br />Intrigued? <br /><br /><b>YOU SHOULD BE. </b><br /><br />Ever since I read <i>Radiance</i> last year, I’ve been on the lookout for more books in the Fantasy Romance subgenre. Which is why I picked this one up. <br /><br />Only…<br /><br />While it’s listed as a fantasy, it has all the trappings of a classic fairy tale. I mean that in the BEST possible way. There are curses, prophecies, evil sorcerers, gallant princes, reluctant princesses, and creatures of all shapes and sizes. <br /><br />I absolutely devoured it, reading it in a single sitting. What can I say? Magic infuses these pages, and I found it damn near impossible to resist Harmon’s spellbinding prose. The world she weaves with her words is as enthralling as it was enchanting, and I’m sorry to leave it behind. <br /><br />HIGHLY RECOMMENDED FOR FAIRY TALE FANS.<br /><br /><b><a href="http://www.thealliterates.com/" rel="nofollow noopener">Blog</a> | <a href="https://www.facebook.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Facebook</a> | <a href="https://twitter.com/thealliterates" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> | <a href="https://www.instagram.com/the_alliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> | <a href="https://www.pinterest.com/thealliterates/" rel="nofollow noopener">Pinterest</a></b></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2291192609" class="readable"

<span id="freeTextContainer12896937283175810392"><blockquote>
  <i>I see you, stars. Do you see me, peeking up through velvet leaves? Keep me safe from mice and men, invisible to all but friends.</i>
</blockquote><br/><br/><br/><a href='https://gifyu.com/image/dXXz' rel='nofollow noopener'>
  <img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586100549i/29236937._SX540_.jpg' alt='banner-di-bobi.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/>
</a><br/><br/><br/>It's official. <br/>I need Amy Harmon to write me bedtime stories and possibly my epitaph, too. <br/><br/><br/>Looking at those ratings and some of you guys' reviews, I guessed The Bird and the Sword to be good. I just never imagined how actually good it would be.<br/>Hence, I'm still pleasantly surprised about how much I ended up liking this. <br/>No, scratch that. <br/>I totally loved it. <br/>I can</span>
  <span id="freeText12896937283175810392" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <i>I see you, stars. Do you see me, peeking up through velvet leaves? Keep me safe from mice and men, invisible to all but friends.</i>
</blockquote><br><br><br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/dXXz" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1586100549i/29236937._SX540_.jpg" alt="banner-di-bobi.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><br>It's official. <br>I need Amy Harmon to write me bedtime stories and possibly my epitaph, too. <br><br><br>Looking at those ratings and some of you guys' reviews, I guessed The Bird and the Sword to be good. I just never imagined how actually good it would be.<br>Hence, I'm still pleasantly surprised about how much I ended up liking this. <br>No, scratch that. <br>I totally loved it. <br>I can't wait for my brain to start working properly again so I can share my reasons with you all. <br><br>Wow. Just, wow. <br><a href="https://gifyu.com/image/Nv1z" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1537628611ra/26337731.gif" alt="source-2.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br>And it might have made it into the top 3 of my all time favorite books. I'm not kidding nor exaggerating; this book is pure awesomeness. <br>I'm honestly a bit disappointed that it's not more recognized, given the original plot, the great characterization of the protagonists, and the way Harmon's words seem to penetrate under your skin. <br>So sad to see how awfully underrated this novel is, when it clearly shouldn't be. <br>I'm in love with <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/author/show/5829056.Amy_Harmon" title="Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Amy Harmon</a>'s whimsical writing and stunningly vivid imagery. <br>This book is and has everything I've ever needed in a story and now I'm out of words. <br>Kind of ironic, considering this book is all about words and the power they behold.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206385.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Professional Reader" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206386.png" width="80" height="80" alt="10 Book Reviews" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1585673329i/29206384.png" width="80" height="80" alt="Reviews Published" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></span>
  <a data-text-id="12896937283175810392" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<span id="freeTextContainer13245944461130263768"><b>4 STARS </b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463332949i/19107229._SY540_.jpg' width='430' height='430' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Amy Harmon delights fans with this well-crafted fantasy tale in which she not only pulls off depicting a whole layered world but does it with such beauty in her words. At times they are spun so poetically and powerful that a reader may lose sight that this is her first fantasy book published. <br/><br/><b>
  <i>"You don't need wings to fly."</i>
</b><br/><br/><span>[image error]</span><br/><br/>The story is told in the first person POV of the heroine, Lark. Lark houses great power in her words however in this land those who have great gifts ar</span>
  <span id="freeText13245944461130263768" style="display:none"><b>4 STARS </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463332949i/19107229._SY540_.jpg" width="430" height="430" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Amy Harmon delights fans with this well-crafted fantasy tale in which she not only pulls off depicting a whole layered world but does it with such beauty in her words. At times they are spun so poetically and powerful that a reader may lose sight that this is her first fantasy book published. <br><br><b>
  <i>"You don't need wings to fly."</i>
</b><br><br><span>[image error]</span><br><br>The story is told in the first person POV of the heroine, Lark. Lark houses great power in her words however in this land those who have great gifts are prosecuted. After the brutal death of her mother at a young age, Lark is left silent until years later when King, Taris claims her. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463332902i/19107222._SY540_.jpg" width="430" height="430" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The story is so cleverly told and paced. The love story of Lark and Taris is scattered with twists and surprises as a reader can’t help but be swept up within Amy Harmon’s gift of words! <br><br><b>
  <i>"You are dangerous little bird. But I think I will keep you." </i>

<div id="review_3440243617" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/3440243617" />
    <a title="Arini" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/39722464-arini"><img alt="Arini" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1565922259p2/39722464.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/3440243617?book_show_action=true">Jul 13, 2020</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Arini" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Arini" href="/user/show/39722464-arini">Arini</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30171592-the-bird-and-the-sword">review of another edition</a>


        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer3440243617" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer6671966635866025764">I’m blessed! When goddess of storytelling bestows upon you a beauty such as this book, it’s going to feel like . . .<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594628270ra/29806377.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>AH’s writing always has a way of making me feel like I’m a child again being cocooned in my mama’s embrace while listening to her soft voice lulling me to sleep with stories of prince and princesses, their wonders, adventures, and magic.<br/><br/>(No kidding. I was kinda being literal considering the prologue and the epilogue scenes were that of a mother and her daughter.) In all seriousness</span>
  <span id="freeText6671966635866025764" style="display:none">I’m blessed! When goddess of storytelling bestows upon you a beauty such as this book, it’s going to feel like . . .<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594628270ra/29806377.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>AH’s writing always has a way of making me feel like I’m a child again being cocooned in my mama’s embrace while listening to her soft voice lulling me to sleep with stories of prince and princesses, their wonders, adventures, and magic.<br><br>(No kidding. I was kinda being literal considering the prologue and the epilogue scenes were that of a mother and her daughter.) In all seriousness, AH’s use of purple prose is one of the few that I can stomach and appreciate the <i>allure</i> of without feeling like I was being smothered.<br><br><b>This time it was no different, for this tale was enchanting, the world building impeccable, the characters relatable, and the romance heartwarming.</b><br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1594646257ra/29807667.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I might be alone in this assessment, but Tiras reminded me of Tamlin and Rhysand. He was somewhere in the middle between both. Meanwhile, I adored Lark. She was special and a badass but in an understated way.<br><br>Honestly, I wasn’t sure about the romance. I mean, being captured and then falling in love with your captor? Yeah, right, sounds familiar. Perfect recipe for a romance, but I also wish they’d fallen in love under different circumstances. Regardless, I loved all the interactions that they had.<br><br>For most of the book, we just saw these characters fighting in a war against beast like creatures with no personality other than being a predator. I didn’t see the plot twist coming, but I wish we’d known about the real <i>villain</i> since the beginning. I think that would’ve made the story more impactful.<br><br>All in all, <i>The Bird and the Sword</i> was stunning even in its flaw. I would recommend for anyone looking for a fantasy romance escape. I’m pretty sure you can read it as a standalone as this one ended conclusively and the next one follows different characters.<br><br><b>
  <i>(Read as an Audiobook)</i>
</b><br><br><b>Thank you for the recommendation!</b> I can’t link all the profiles, but I see YOU and this was very much appreciated. Also, to those who are interested, if you can’t rely on my review, see below and it should tell you this is a book you wanna read or not.<br><br><b>List of similar books:</b><br>↠ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/24473763.Radiance__Wraith_Kings___1_" title="Radiance (Wraith Kings, #1) by Grace Draven" rel="nofollow noopener">Radiance</a><br>↠ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/43204703.A_Curse_So_Dark_and_Lonely__Cursebreakers___1_" title="A Curse So Dark and Lonely (Cursebreakers, #1) by Brigid Kemmerer" rel="nofollow noopener">A Curse So Dark and Lonely</a><br>↠ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/52831200.From_Blood_and_Ash__Blood_And_Ash___1_" title="From Blood and Ash (Blood And Ash, #1) by Jennifer L. Armentrout" rel="nofollow noopener">From Blood and Ash</a><br>↠ <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/7896527.Throne_of_Glass__Throne_of_Glass___1_" title="Throne of Glass (Throne of Glass, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">ToG</a>/<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/16096824.A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses__A_Court_of_Thorns_and_Roses___1_" title="A Court of Thorns and Roses (A Court of Thorns and Roses, #1) by Sarah J. Maas" rel="nofollow noopener">ACOTAR</a></span>

I've been trying to catch up on reading her recent releases and boy am I glad I finally got to this book. It is gripping, fantastically written and with a surprisingly well-rounded world building for being a standalone. <br/><br/>➦This fantasy romance follows a journey of Lark, a young mute woman, who has been cursed by h</span>
  <span id="freeText10584404973222977189" style="display:none">You can win this on Audio!!! There's till time to enter this giveaway on the front page of <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.steamyreads.net">www.steamyreads.net</a> <br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1499269202i/23211502._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1479146098i/21153583.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1492734928i/22548392._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br>➦I've been a fan on Amy Harmon's writing ever since I've read <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/27237358.Making_Faces" title="Making Faces by Amy Harmon" rel="nofollow noopener">Making Faces</a>. I've been trying to catch up on reading her recent releases and boy am I glad I finally got to this book. It is gripping, fantastically written and with a surprisingly well-rounded world building for being a standalone. <br><br>➦This fantasy romance follows a journey of Lark, a young mute woman, who has been cursed by her mother to stay silent. In the land where magic is frown upon and is punishable by death, Lark realizes that she is to remain quiet for her own protection. So what happens when she becomes a prisoner to the king and gets exposed to books? Will she discover the power of words?<br><br>➦The poetic tone is what I come to expect from Harmon's writing and it is very prominent in this particular book. A lot of prophecies are in rhymes and I was completely fascinated by them. The romance aspect is very prominent and the author certainly took the time developing the romantic relationship.<br><br>➦If you like Sarah J. Maas' books then you will probably enjoy this one. It has plenty of romance as well as constant action. If you love all things magic - the future telling, the healing, the changing into beastly creatures, then you should definitely give this one a chance. Also, it's nice to be able to just read a fantasy standalone. There will be other books in this series set in the same world but, looks like, about other couples. I will be reading all of them.<br><a href="https://www.facebook.com/SteamyReadsBlog/" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1927560161" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1927560161" />
    <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink"><img alt="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1568991289p2/50044222.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1927560161?book_show_action=true">Feb 28, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink" href="/user/show/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink">Brittney ~ Reverie and Ink</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=favorite-heroines">favorite-heroines</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/50044222-brittney-reverie-and-ink?shelf=recommended-fantasy">recommended-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1927560161" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12844035410091006888">First of all, I want to comment on the writing. It was breathtaking, like reading poetry or listening to violins while smelling roses. <br/><br/>I was hooked from the very start, and quickly got lost in a very good way. The intro might even be my favorite part - folklore meets fairytale and completely intriguing. I mean c'mon, you ready something like below... how can you not read more?<br/><br/><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them </b></i></blockquote></span>
  <span id="freeText12844035410091006888" style="display:none">First of all, I want to comment on the writing. It was breathtaking, like reading poetry or listening to violins while smelling roses. <br /><br />I was hooked from the very start, and quickly got lost in a very good way. The intro might even be my favorite part - folklore meets fairytale and completely intriguing. I mean c'mon, you ready something like below... how can you not read more?<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b>“Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them 'til they've time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, 'til the hour. You won't speak and you won't tell, you won't call on heav'n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, daughter. Stay alive.” </b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />Honestly the whole thing reads like an old-timey fairytale - full of beauty, mystery, and darkness. Lark (yep, that's the MC's name and its totally awesome) can't speak, thanks to a curse her mother meant to protect her when she was young - as you can tell if you read the above quote. In fact, it all happens right before her mother is killed by the king for having magic. <br /><br />When Lark grows up (at the start of the novel), we find out very quickly how sad her life is. Not only can she not speak, but her father holds no love for her and sees her only as a waste, a curse. He'd like nothing more than to be rid of her, but the second part of Lark's mother's curse is that their lives are tied together. He will die if something happens to her. So, Lark is kept at his manor for 'safekeeping'. Her father won't allow her to learn to read or write, much less anything else. <br /><br />Everything changes when the son of the man who killed her mother, the current king, shows up and whisks her away (I won't explain why.) <br /><br />I'd say just go in not knowing much more than that. The story is very much driven by emotion. Having the story told from Lark's perspective is so interesting - we learn how she feels just by her inner monologue and how she gestures to people since she is unable to speak herself. And when she captures the attention of the king and the two start to get to know each other, things get even more emotional. I'm pretty sure I shed a few tears in this one.<br /><br /><blockquote>
  <i>
    <b><br />I couldn’t explain how it felt to converse with another human being. To actually converse. I had been reduced to sharing nothing of my innermost thoughts for most of my life. Reduced to throwing things when I was angry. Reduced to tears when I was sad. Reduced to the simplicity of nods and bows, of having people look away from me or become frustrated when they didn’t know what I was trying to communicate.</b>
  </i>
</blockquote><br /><br />The ending was really beautiful. Though a generally sad book, I felt really satisfied at the conclusion (I was really getting worried there for a while.) I'd recommend this to fans of Naomi Novak or Grace Draven! <br /><br />My biggest complaint is the very strange nods to Christianity. Normally I'd be all for that, but it just felt too weird, almost like copying to an extent and then warping it. For example, in the beginning, the author literally describes how the world is made and she straight up took it from Genesis (almost <u>word for word</u> )... up until she decided she wanted it to stop and formed into some other form of religion. Then, she uses several biblical references such as 'two-edged sword' and whatnot. <br /><br />Again, it wasn't that I minded that referenced it or anything like that.. but it just felt cheap the way she handled it. I'm curious if someone else felt this way. It would be one thing if she gave credit or talked about her inspiration in the acknowledgements or just SOMEWHERE, but I searched and searched and found nothing. I love seeing real life inspiration and how it can breath into a story but this just felt... wrong.<br /><br />Either way, I enjoyed the book and I'm stoked for the sequel (though thank goodness this one wrapped up for the most part!) <br /><br /><a href="http://www.herbookishthings.com" rel="nofollow noopener">My Blog</a> ~ <a href="https://www.instagram.com/herbookishthings/" rel="nofollow noopener">Instagram</a> ~ <a href="https://twitter.com/herbookishthing" rel="nofollow noopener">Twitter</a> ~ <a href="https://www.etsy.com/shop/herbookishthings" rel="nofollow noopener">Etsy</a></span>
  <a data-text-id="12844035410091006888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1830269679?book_show_action=true">Dec 05, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">

        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30171592-the-bird-and-the-sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=paranormal-romance">paranormal-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=ebooks">ebooks</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=werewolves-shapeshifters">werewolves-shapeshifters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/14514998-rachel-reads-ravenously?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>
          </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1830269679" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3271268796137552220"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br/><br/><b> <i> “Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them 'til they've time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, 'til the hour. You won't speak and you won't tell, you won't call on heav'n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, daughter. Stay alive.” </i> </b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481096358i/21383712._SX540_.png' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Amy Harmon just has this way with words, she infuses beauty into them. She takes words and gives them substance, she makes them pretty.<br/><br/>The</span>
  <span id="freeText3271268796137552220" style="display:none"><b> 4.5 stars! </b><br><br><b> <i> “Swallow Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them 'til they've time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, 'til the hour. You won't speak and you won't tell, you won't call on heav'n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive. Silence, daughter. Stay alive.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481096358i/21383712._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Amy Harmon just has this way with words, she infuses beauty into them. She takes words and gives them substance, she makes them pretty.<br><br>The Bird and the Sword is a high fantasy novel following a young woman named Lark. When she was a child her mother died to protect her, taking the fall for an ability Lark has so that Lark would not be killed. Now grown, Lark has not spoken since the day her mother died and she is heavily protected by her father. When King Tiras comes and takes Lark as collateral, Lark is swept away to a new place, one where she learns more than she ever could before.<br><br>Words are her power, and the knowledge of words was kept from her until now. And Tiras becomes aware of Lark's power and needs it to help save everyone's lives. But can Lark save Tiras from his own curse?<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1458616698i/18508485.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b> <i> “You glow, Lark.” His hand climbed back up again and swept over my unbound hair. I swallowed, suddenly close to tears. Then why does no one see me? “I see you,” he said.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1481096358i/21383713._SX540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>I loved this book. Plain and simple. Harmon's work can be a hit or a miss for me, before this book it was about a 50/50 split on the 4 books I had already read. I am a huge fantasy fan so despite my reservations I was intrigued. On top of that so many people have recommended this book and I basically waved them on, putting it off even longer. <br><br>As of late I have have trouble finding a romance novel that is worth my time, that doesn't sound like everything else out there. THIS is that book, the one that is so uniquely special it blows all other books out of the water. Harmon's magical writing style, not once did I skim, not once did I want to put the book down and I stayed up until 2 am finishing this novel. For a woman who normally writes contemporary, she nailed the world building required for a high fantasy novel. The imagery was stunning, I felt as if I was in this world myself.<br><br>So if you are hesitant to read this book for any reason, I say let your reservations go and try it anyway. That's what I did, and it worked out wonderfully for me.<br><br><b> <i> “I think I will keep you.” </i> </b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1455783307i/18148833._SX540_.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"> </span>
  <a data-text-id="3271268796137552220" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

<div id="review_1543011153" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1543011153" />
    <a title="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover"><img alt="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489089790p2/34338862.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1543011153?book_show_action=true">Feb 09, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" class="user" itemprop="url" name="TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover" href="/user/show/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover">TheCrazyWorldOfABookLover</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30171592-the-bird-and-the-sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/34338862-thecrazyworldofabooklover?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1543011153" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer1846543333228616465"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You are a dangerous little bird. But I think I will keep you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463784205i/19159372._SY540_.jpg' width='450' height='450' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>WHAT A BEAUTIFUL STORY!!<br/><br/>Without revealing too much, it’ll be hard to go into the plot of this story and what it’s all about, so I won't say much. And as always, when I read an incredible book it's so hard to do the book justice and convey just how epic the story was with my words.<br/><br/>But I can say Amy's writing is nothing short of magical, and I was immediately swept up into the story of Lark and Tiras. And on top of the bea</span>
  <span id="freeText1846543333228616465" style="display:none"><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“You are a dangerous little bird. But I think I will keep you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote> <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463784205i/19159372._SY540_.jpg" width="450" height="450" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>WHAT A BEAUTIFUL STORY!!<br><br>Without revealing too much, it’ll be hard to go into the plot of this story and what it’s all about, so I won't say much. And as always, when I read an incredible book it's so hard to do the book justice and convey just how epic the story was with my words.<br><br>But I can say Amy's writing is nothing short of magical, and I was immediately swept up into the story of Lark and Tiras. And on top of the beautiful romance, there was mystery, intrigue, and an elaborate plot that kept me completely immersed from start to finish.<br><br>Everything about this was original, poignant, and brilliant. And while there is very little sex, this story was oozing with <b>sensuality and romance.</b> The story of Lark and Tiras is one I will not forget and probably one of the most romantic stories I have come across. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Yearning. There it was again. Suddenly yearning had a flavor. It tasted like a king, a beautiful, frightening, infuriating man who flew into my life and began to free my words."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>There were SO MANY lines and passages I just had to highlight and wish I could share here. But then this review would be insanely lomg and you should be reading the book and experiencing it for yourself. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"You are easy to overlook. Slim and pale and so quiet. But now that I've studied your soft grey eyes and traced the fine bones of your face, now that I've kissed your pale pink mouth, I don't want to look anywhere else. My gaze is continually drawn back to you."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>I know this is fantasy and a lot of people shy away from this genre. But DO NOT let that dissuade you from picking this up. Trust me when I tell you ANYONE that likes romance NEEDS to read this story. <br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>“I have loved you every moment of every day, and I will love you until I cease to be. Bird, man, or king, I love you, and I will always love you.”</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><b>Put simply, this was stunning.</b> And I cannot recommend it enough. <br><br><a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://amzn.to/20gZHhw">http://amzn.to/20gZHhw</a><br><br><a href="https://thecrazyworldofabooklover.wordpress.com/" target="blog" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1467902722i/19644381._SX540_.jpg" width="275" height="150" class="gr-hostedUserImg">

<div id="review_1918897844" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1918897844" />
    <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee"><img alt="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1583262285p2/44137919.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1918897844?book_show_action=true">Feb 24, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Mikee (ReadWithMikee)" href="/user/show/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee">Mikee (ReadWithMikee)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30171592-the-bird-and-the-sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/44137919-mikee-readwithmikee?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1918897844" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7492995273749021384"><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488090469i/22079784._SY540_.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝I have loved you every moment of every day, and I will love you until I cease to be. Bird, man, or king, I love you, and I will always love you.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br/><br/>Okay let me just take second to say thank you to Milana from A Couple Reads because she's amazing and she's the one who got me to pick up this book. And let me just say, I was blown away by how much I actually enjoyed The Bird and the Sword. I haven't wrote a proper review in a long time but I just have to write one for this book because I </span>
  <span id="freeText7492995273749021384" style="display:none"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1488090469i/22079784._SY540_.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>❝I have loved you every moment of every day, and I will love you until I cease to be. Bird, man, or king, I love you, and I will always love you.❞</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br>Okay let me just take second to say thank you to Milana from A Couple Reads because she's amazing and she's the one who got me to pick up this book. And let me just say, I was blown away by how much I actually enjoyed The Bird and the Sword. I haven't wrote a proper review in a long time but I just have to write one for this book because I strongly believe that more people should give The Bird and the Sword a try!<br><br>At first, I was a bit hesitant about this book. I was familiar with Amy Harmon but I've actually never read any of her books. I knew her as an NA contemporary romance author rather than a fantasy author so I wasn't sure what to expect. Do I go in warily knowing that Amy Harmon isn't exactly a fantasy author like Sarah J. Maas or Leigh Bardugo, or any other author that writes only and primarily fantasy? Or do I give her the benefit of the doubt and give her and this book a chance? I chose the latter because it's not everyday an author steps out of their usual genre to try and tackle one that's completely on the opposite side of their spectrum. And let me tell you, I MADE THE RIGHT CHOICE.<br><br>Although The Bird and the Sword is set in a fantasy world, I found that it was very light fantasy. I'm a huge high fantasy reader. I love complex characters and worldbuilding. But sometimes those types of books get super dense and we need to take a break from heavy books every once in awhile while staying within our preferred genres, and I believe that The Bird and the Sword is perfect for someone looking for a light, quick, fantasy read. The worldbuilding wasn't complex and was easy to follow. It was simple and you didn't need to pick it apart and put the pieces together just to understand what's going on. There was a simple hierarchy of the different gifts and that's all you really need to know.<br><br>As for the main characters in the story, Lark was a decent heroine. She wasn't really anything special from the typical female character but I did love her gifted abilities! The character that did steal the show was definitely Tiras. I LOVE TIRAS. My heart broke so many times throughout this book because of him and I know I wouldn't have loved this book as much as I do if it wasn't for Tiras. His storyline reminded me so much of Beauty and the Beast. Instead of the Beast turning back into a man, it's man turning into Beast.<br><br>In terms of romance, I didn't love the relationship between Lark and Tiras as much as I wanted to. To be honest, I actually didn't really buy into their romance but as the story progressed my heart still ached for the both of them and what they had to endure together and individually. I didn't really feel sparks flying but I was satisfied with how their relationship developed.<br><br>Overall, I was pleasantly surprised with how The Bird and the Sword played out. I wasn't expecting anything higher than a 3-Star read but I was definitely hooked. There were some slow parts here and there but the last hundred pages or so really made up for it. My heart wouldn't stop falling apart and putting itself back together so many times towards the end. Amy Harmon really blew me away with this one and I would really love to see more fantasy books from her!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7492995273749021384" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <u>The Bird and the Sword</u>
</b> was a beautiful tale about a time when Kings and Queens reigned and magical powers embodied the land. <br/><br/><u><b>"I wasn't safe, the king was cursed, and the world was upside down."</b> </u><br/>Now, that's a storyline to get the heart pumping. I don't want to ruin this phenomenal tale by sharing what the book is about but I will say this is another <b>must read</b> book by Amy Harmon. The reading world is blessed to have an author like her whose ability to create both unique and dee</span>
  <span id="freeText7500857790848857092" style="display:none"><b>Words evade me!</b> <br><br><b>
  <u>The Bird and the Sword</u>
</b> was a beautiful tale about a time when Kings and Queens reigned and magical powers embodied the land. <br><br><u><b>"I wasn't safe, the king was cursed, and the world was upside down."</b> </u><br>Now, that's a storyline to get the heart pumping. I don't want to ruin this phenomenal tale by sharing what the book is about but I will say this is another <b>must read</b> book by Amy Harmon. The reading world is blessed to have an author like her whose ability to create both unique and deeply meaningful stories has enriched the romance world.<br><br><b>STANDALONE</b><br><br><a href="http://foxyblogs.com" rel="nofollow noopener">

<div id="review_1626264273" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1626264273" />
    <a title="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts"><img alt="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1591195447p2/16496589.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1626264273?book_show_action=true">May 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts" href="/user/show/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts">Jx PinkLady Reviews ♡ @bookwormthoughts</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/16496589-jx-pinklady-reviews-bookwormthoughts?shelf=advance-copy">advance-copy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1626264273" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8506274309399085026"><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463349772i/19108820._SX540_.jpg' width='400' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/> THE BIRD AND THE SWORD is a STANDALONE Fantasy Romance story about a beautiful, gifted, kind, caring and quiet girl called Lark and the King of Jeru. Told from the first person narrative of Lark, the world showcased is one of true fantasy, a world with magic and populated by warriors and people with powers, some would call gifts, others something quite different. A mesmerizing story with heart, soul and magic that depicts the importance and the power of words both spoken and unspoken. The Bird </span>
  <span id="freeText8506274309399085026" style="display:none"><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463349772i/19108820._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br> THE BIRD AND THE SWORD is a STANDALONE Fantasy Romance story about a beautiful, gifted, kind, caring and quiet girl called Lark and the King of Jeru. Told from the first person narrative of Lark, the world showcased is one of true fantasy, a world with magic and populated by warriors and people with powers, some would call gifts, others something quite different. A mesmerizing story with heart, soul and magic that depicts the importance and the power of words both spoken and unspoken. The Bird and the Sword is simply an incredibly compelling read that reached into my heart and made me feel so much for the magical world and the gifted characters that dwell there. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463343297i/19108253._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Produced with a sprinkle of magic, not only in the subject matter, but in the expertly crafted, rich and thought provoking manner in which the story is showcased. The depth ridden hypnotic prose is lyrical and poetic evoking beautiful feelings of love, satisfaction and beauty. It’s about freedom, acceptance, fear, survival and love all ensconced in a fantasy world of magic and power. The enchanting story has an old world feel beginning with a prologue that's eerie, surprising, pulled on my heart and set the tone and theme of this romantic fantasy to perfection, drawing me in and capturing my full fascination with this story and its characters. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463343297i/19108252._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The emerging world and dynamic protagonists evoked my smiles, laughter and tears within a writing canvas that slowly builds to an exquisite, romantic and fierce story of love, strength and adventure. There are twists and turns throughout the story arc that ensured my rapt attention and developed my feelings of love for the tale. The romantic aspect combined with the themes and their portrayals completely swept me away as each element weaves with another ultimately producing a dramatic climax that had my heart aching for the possibilities and swelling with love. <br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463407890i/19115141._SX540_.jpg" width="400" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The fairy tale world created by Amy Harmon enchanted me, made me believe in their world and feel for the protagonists. Their love story is gentle and pure and totally enamoured my heart. Fantasy Romance is not a genre I would usually select but any book written by this author is bound to be special and unique and this story measures up in abundance. It is thought provoking, honest, and magical and I felt an overwhelming sense of contentment as I absorbed the lyrical prose and lost myself in the world depicted. I highly recommend this story to all ROMANCE readers who appreciate depth ridden, richly beautiful writing with heart and soul. <br><br><br>Advance copy provided for my honest review thoughts <br><br>★ Graphics created by myself with free stock image from Pexels and stock image I purchased from deposit photos ★</span>
  <a data-text-id="8506274309399085026" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>

<span id="freeTextContainer1844063735422021612"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463508893i/19126667._SX540_.jpg' width='400' height='267' alt='description' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Amy Harmon never fails when it comes to spinning beautiful words. I have yet to pick up one of her creations and not marvel at her storytelling ability. And yet again, she has weaved a story unlike any other I've read. a fantastical world full of magic, secrets, fear, and courage. I can't see fans of the fantasy genre not enjoying the romance and adventure found within the story of Lark and Tiras. Admittedly, it did take me a few days to read <i>The Bird and the Sword</i>, but that in no way i</span>
  <span id="freeText1844063735422021612" style="display:none"><b>4.5 Stars</b><br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1463508893i/19126667._SX540_.jpg" width="400" height="267" alt="description" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Amy Harmon never fails when it comes to spinning beautiful words. I have yet to pick up one of her creations and not marvel at her storytelling ability. And yet again, she has weaved a story unlike any other I've read. a fantastical world full of magic, secrets, fear, and courage. I can't see fans of the fantasy genre not enjoying the romance and adventure found within the story of Lark and Tiras. Admittedly, it did take me a few days to read <i>The Bird and the Sword</i>, but that in no way is a reflection of dislike/disinterest in the story, only, that I have been struggling to find the time/attention to read. <br><br>Full review to come...<br>hopefully, if not - I really enjoyed this one. </span>

<div id="review_1643374649" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1643374649" />
    <a title="Snow" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/31719636-snow"><img alt="Snow" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1465808156p2/31719636.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1643374649?book_show_action=true">May 19, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Snow" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Snow" href="/user/show/31719636-snow">Snow</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31719636-snow?shelf=action">action</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31719636-snow?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31719636-snow?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31719636-snow?shelf=favorites">favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31719636-snow?shelf=magic">magic</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31719636-snow?shelf=best-ever">best-ever</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31719636-snow?shelf=5-star-read">5-star-read</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/31719636-snow?shelf=best-in-2016">best-in-2016</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1643374649" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4137345552865881042"><b>6 "silent words" stars</b><br/><br/>These segments of the blurb, will tease you…<br/><br/><i>
  <blockquote>The day my mother was killed, she told my father I wouldn’t speak again, and she told him if I died, he would die too…<br/><br/>She predicted the king would trade his soul and lose his son to the sky…<br/><br/>My father has a claim to the throne, and he is waiting in the shadows…<br/><br/>I just want to be free.<br/><br/>But freedom will require escape, and I’m a prisoner of my mother’s curse and my father’s greed….<br/><br/>I can’t speak or make a sound…<br/><br/>In a land purged of en</blockquote></i></span>
  <span id="freeText4137345552865881042" style="display:none"><b>6 "silent words" stars</b><br><br>These segments of the blurb, will tease you…<br><br><i>
  <blockquote>The day my mother was killed, she told my father I wouldn’t speak again, and she told him if I died, he would die too…<br><br>She predicted the king would trade his soul and lose his son to the sky…<br><br>My father has a claim to the throne, and he is waiting in the shadows…<br><br>I just want to be free.<br><br>But freedom will require escape, and I’m a prisoner of my mother’s curse and my father’s greed….<br><br>I can’t speak or make a sound…<br><br>In a land purged of enchantment, love might be the only magic left, and who could ever love . . . a bird?</blockquote>
</i><br><br>It will make you say…wait, what? Is this a fable? <br><br><b>And I would promptly say YES! <br>It's the most beautiful story of MAGIC, POWER and LOVE, overcoming the differencies, the odds, the misfortune, the pain, the diversities that change to course of essence of life and love as you know it.</b><br><br>Once upon a time, a magical world existed where the <i>GIFTED</i> lived among the common people in togetherness and unity.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>The mouth, the hand, the heart, and the eye – the Teller, the Spinner, the Healer and the Changer.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Until greed, hunger for power, deceit and treachery overruled the GIFTED as the EVIL ones and ruled them out, estinguishing them and punishing them for being sorcerers.<br><br><b>Lady Lark of Corvyn</b> was born into a noble family but she was also a gifted one. Being her mother's daughter, who was a powerful TELLER, she witnessed her mother's death by the hand of a King. But before she died, she placed the curse on them all. Changing the destiny, binding the souls together by a silent power of an unsaid word.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i> Swallow, Daughter, pull them in, those words that sit upon your lips. Lock them deep inside your soul, hide them ‘til they’ve time to grow. Close your mouth upon the power, curse not, cure not, ‘til the hour. You won’t speak and you won’t tell, you won’t call on heav’n or hell. You will learn and you will thrive.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Cause <br><br><b>
  <i>Silence was a close cousin to invisibility.</i>
</b><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>"Silence, Daughter. Stay alive."</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Lark grew into a shadow.<br><br><a href="http://s482.photobucket.com/user/SnowCat79/media/da3ac00d-18cb-49c2-991a-8811f82c3187_zps1ls6cvcr.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464015766i/19185731._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo da3ac00d-18cb-49c2-991a-8811f82c3187_zps1ls6cvcr.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Neglected and left aside, people dismissed her as mute and therefore not worthy. All she wanted was to be free.<br><br><a href="http://s482.photobucket.com/user/SnowCat79/media/9c27065a-6164-4010-af3e-ef505bcc5d94_zps7788sbgq.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464015766i/19185732._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo 9c27065a-6164-4010-af3e-ef505bcc5d94_zps7788sbgq.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>BUT she was so much more inside her silence.<br><br><a href="http://s482.photobucket.com/user/SnowCat79/media/lark1_zpsolrh8ntl.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464015766i/19185733._SY540_.jpg" alt=" photo lark1_zpsolrh8ntl.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>Her inner power of silent words was immense as it will be soon proven as useful when she becomes the interest of a young <b>King Tiras</b> and a means to an end. Not knowing the real destined bond/a curse binding Lark with her father, King Tiras takes her as his prisoner forcing her father to act as in providing the King much needed army to end the war with Volgars, devious creatures – half men/half birds, who were dangerously close to destroying the precious Jeru Kingdom.<br><br><a href="http://s482.photobucket.com/user/SnowCat79/media/5b4fe7a4-404a-49c7-8361-129c526c8dde_zpsckrwzs3q.jpg.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1464015766i/19185734._SX540_.jpg" alt=" photo 5b4fe7a4-404a-49c7-8361-129c526c8dde_zpsckrwzs3q.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br>King Tiras soon finds out that Lark is more than she appears to be…she could help him subsiding his own troubled physical pain as he holds a terrible secret that could destroy and shattered him if it should ever become known. / <i>Mikiya. Eagle.</i><br>…but Lark's power were silent words…<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>I wasn't healing. I was telling. I was suggesting. Commanding his body to release the pain, to numb the agony. To heal itself.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>Tiras and Lark become close, he opens her to another world, the world that was „closed off“ for so long and she craved for it. She wanted to learn, she swallowed her words but she needed to hear them, she wanted to grasp the meaning of the sound and to give it essence.<br>What they shared was not planned, was not expected either.<br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>„You are easy to overlook. Slim and pale and so quiet. But now that I've studied your soft grey eyes and traced the fine bones of your face, now that I've kissed your pale pink mouth, I don't want to look anywhere else. My gaze is continually drawn back to you.“</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br>But the longer they spend time together, they grow into each other, trusting, providing safety and belonging…it was beyond physical, it was beyond words…and yet their connection was magic itself.<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1464015766ra/19185735.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><blockquote>
  <b>
    <i>„I'm going to kiss you again“<br>„Unless you tell me no.“<br>My mind was a huge, white wall. No protestations. No thoughts. No words at all.</i>
  </b>
</blockquote><br><br><a href="http://s482.photobucket.com/user/SnowCat79/media/19185737__SY540__zps42u14thc.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener">
  <img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486542928i/21925159._SY540_.png" alt=" photo 19185737__SY540__zps42u14thc.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg">
</a><br><br><blockquote>
<b><i>The way Tiras was looking at me made me believe I was vibrant and brave. He made me feel powerful.</i></b><br>The fear of letting go, to break free fully is terrifying and Lark is holding back until the inevitable sets in place…<br><blockquote><b><i>I have all the power, but you will destroy me. <br>„Only your walls, Lark.“<br>„I need you to let me in.“<br>If I let you in, I will have nothing left. If I am like ice it is because ice is impenetrable. Strong.</i></b></blockquote>
<br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1449013602ra/17220454.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><blockquote><b><i>„Touch me, Lark.“<br>When I touch you, I cease to be.<br>Why do you want so badly to break me?<br>„Because there is fire beneath the ice, Lark. And I like your fire.“</i></b></blockquote>
<br><br><a href="http://s482.photobucket.com/user/SnowCat79/media/bird_zpschfabdqx.png.html" target="_blank" rel="nofollow noopener"><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1486543612i/21925238._SY540_.png" alt=" photo bird_zpschfabdqx.png" class="gr-hostedUserImg"></a><br><blockquote><b><i>„Then I think I will keep you.“</i></b></blockquote>
<br><br><b>Phenomenal writing, fantastic story with even more thrilling and captivating characters! Lyrical, methaphorical lines that speak louder than any volume, words that have a meaning only when you give them one.</b><br><blockquote><b><i>You don't need wings to fly…<br>What do you need…<br>Words.</i></b></blockquote>
<br><br><b>One of the best books I have read this year! <br><br>Absolutely stunning and beautiful story...<br><br>This one will stay with me for a long time....</b><br><br><i><blockquote>"It's only words, and words are all i have to take your heart away..."</blockquote></i>
</blockquote> <br><i>
  <b>Words</b>
</i> by Bee Gees</span>
  <a data-text-id="4137345552865881042" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1679957987?book_show_action=true">Feb 12, 2017</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Shelly Strange" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Shelly Strange" href="/user/show/25393430-shelly-strange">Shelly Strange</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Kindle Edition " href="/book/show/30171592-the-bird-and-the-sword">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=this-book-is-everything">this-book-is-everything</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy-romance">fantasy-romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=dis-is-a-rully-good-lurv-story">dis-is-a-rully-good-lurv-story</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=fantasy">fantasy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=read-2017">read-2017</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=5-stars">5-stars</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/25393430-shelly-strange?shelf=hot-guys-alphas-rawr">hot-guys-alphas-rawr</a>,

          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1679957987" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer18179418982779121402">I read this for the 2017 <a href='https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read' rel='nofollow noopener'>MacHalo Group</a> Reading Challenge.<br/><br/><img src='https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506286480i/24003492.jpg' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>Review:<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486930207ra/21962090.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/><b>Dis book, guys.</b> My favorite book of the year so far. Maybe my favorite fantasy romance of ALL TIME. <br/><br/>Tirus. I LURVE him. In the harem you go! <br/><br/>Lark was fabulous as the heroine. The author did a fantastic job because Lark was mute for about 95% of the book. <br/><br/>Lots of magic and gifts/abilities. I love that kind of stuff. Healers, shifters, tellers, seers... they are persecuted and hunted, hiding. <br/><br/>It's a world of castles and swords, villag</span>
  <span id="freeText18179418982779121402" style="display:none">I read this for the 2017 <a href="https://www.goodreads.com/group/show/148935-dust-off-your-machalo-it-s-time-for-another-buddy-read" rel="nofollow noopener">MacHalo Group</a> Reading Challenge.<br><br><img src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1506286480i/24003492.jpg" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>Review:<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1486930207ra/21962090.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br><b>Dis book, guys.</b> My favorite book of the year so far. Maybe my favorite fantasy romance of ALL TIME. <br><br>Tirus. I LURVE him. In the harem you go! <br><br>Lark was fabulous as the heroine. The author did a fantastic job because Lark was mute for about 95% of the book. <br><br>Lots of magic and gifts/abilities. I love that kind of stuff. Healers, shifters, tellers, seers... they are persecuted and hunted, hiding. <br><br>It's a world of castles and swords, villagers and noblemen. The romance was awesome. Just the best. I swooned. I cried. I swooned some more. <br><br>Kjell, as the King's half brother. I even liked that grumpypants. And Boojohni, the lovable loyal troll and friend to Lark. <br><br>Dang, but this book was just so good. I highly recommend. Read it! (If you like Grace Draven's stuff, you'll probably like this.)<br><br>If anyone can recommend any other books similar to this, PLEASE DO!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!!<br><br>My only issue (and this is a big spoiler so don't read if you intend to read this book and haven't yet: <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[ The one female who could have been a great friend was made into the villain. I didn't like that. I wanted her to be the friend, not the evil villainy villain. Oh well. <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></["br"]></span>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('FNUCNMr1yYR0oWkbV90YpulgyLGL0wr0OizsAdYr2vhPO8Gb8qA23HkirZ2a+kINTeeGFwc7FI0TrLsZmvWwUg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('NHfWqlyc+S3TU3sO2DVtoPY/x/2Mgs1mvsePob8bU/9vmRUFZMkGdd7Qv4gVEjcLUriJWwBq0x+XR9i588U5VQ==')})
  }

<span id="freeTextContainer3585930507484960742">Amy Harmon is a Wall Street Journal, USA Today, and New York Times Bestselling author. Amy knew at an early age that writing was something she wanted to do, and she divided her time between writing songs and stories as she grew. Having grown up in the middle of wheat fields without a television, with only her books and her siblings to entertain her, she developed a strong sense of what made a good</span>
  <span id="freeText3585930507484960742" style="display:none">Amy Harmon is a Wall Street Journal, USA Today, and New York Times Bestselling author. Amy knew at an early age that writing was something she wanted to do, and she divided her time between writing songs and stories as she grew. Having grown up in the middle of wheat fields without a television, with only her books and her siblings to entertain her, she developed a strong sense of what made a good story. Her books are now being published in eighteen languages, truly a dream come true for a little country girl from Levan, Utah.<br /><br />Amy Harmon has written fifteen novels including the USA Today Bestsellers, Making Faces and Running Barefoot, as well as The Law of Moses, Infinity + One and the New York Times Bestseller, A Different Blue. Her fantasy novel, The Bird and the Sword, was a Goodreads Book of the Year finalist. Her newest release, What the Wind Knows, is an Amazon charts bestseller. For updates on upcoming book releases, author posts and more, join Amy at <a target="_blank" rel="noopener nofollow" href="http://www.authoramyharmon.com">www.authoramyharmon.com</a>.</span>
